B. Material Processed

In October, the Statton was provided by the LIENVOY LP with 13s

pages uf dally resumes from all lines, lo pages of resumes from the Cuban

lines, 17 pages from the Czech lines and 121 pages froin the Soviet lules.

In addition the taped reels from the Soviet and Cauch Iines were turned over

for the transcription.of the Russian and Czech conversatlong. There were

also provided 11 pleces of other miscellancous material.

C. Liaison

Because of the urgeicy of business during the munth of Ocivier, the

COS met with LIERGO and LIELEGANT more frequently, LITENSOR er-

pressed his gratefulness through LIELEGANT on providing him with ropores:

on the political scene in the Far List countries that he had visited, On 25

Ocrober, LITENSOR was given the report on the Cuban sluation which was

sent to the Station in DIR 44302. LITENSOR was also shown photos df the

Soviet missile bases in Cuba. After meering with high-lovel Mexican erticials,

the Chief of Siation reported in MEXI 2397 on their attitudes of the U.S..

quarantine of Cuba and the stopping of further progreds on Soviet missile

bases there.

attompt of Vicente Lombardo Toledano, prominent leftlet Mexican politician,:

to make an appointment witl the Mexican Government In regard to Cubu,

Lombardo 'Toledano was prompred by General Lazaro Cardenas to try co

influence the President. (see MEXI 2402)

quarters on 19 Ocrober to plan with Headquarter's personnel the seiting up of

the new LIENVOY LP.

REFERENCE:

Chief, WH/3

CW Signals on Telephone Tap

HMMA-14977, 18 May 1960

1. A technical analysis of referonce tap indicates that the

CW Morse signals probably were picked up incidental to the primary

cap and did not actually occur on Line #2. This is borne out both

from a technical standpoint (signal to noiso ratio, uxtraneous CW

signals, etc.) as well as from the context of the massages them-

selves.

The latter, as will be noted in the attached tranecript,

primarily concern arrivals and departures of what appear to be

small maritime vossols. The two radio calls mentioned, i. o.

"XBRB2" and "XBRP", are listed in tie International Call Sign

Book as follows:

XBRB - Vera Cruz (19-10N, 90-15 W)

XBRP - Pichilingue (24-12N, 110-20 W)

The originating station in this case was Pichilingue.

Hady safestore is some good reason why a port.

authority on the west coast of Mexico would be sending traffic of

this nature to an east coast port. However, jyns how these

particular signals happenod to be picked up on'

Sim Brooks" lino

is open to conjecturo, It is our guess shat it probably was due

to one of the following reasons:

. A radio transmitter may be situated near the

tap and is serving as a rolay station between Pichiling:

and Vera Cruz, II this is the case it may bo giving off

strong radio frequency signals which possibly are being

rectified by the tap itself,

SEGMET

---

## Page 184

aline:

- 2=

The equipment used in conjunction with the tap

may be serving as a poor radio receiver, using the telephone

Line as au antenna.

ca The CW signals pussibly are being picked up

inductively, i.e. from anosier phone line which is in

iloso proximity to Line 8?. This theory seems unlikely,

however, since the transmission of CW signals from on

coast to the other via telephone lines would be a slow and

impractical procedure.

so from the cantain fee cinical interost, sorter

appreciate being advised if and wten the

appreciate on he bore and when their be do sub-

furnish additional analysis and transcripts should similar signals

Do noted in the future.

WILLIAN K. HARVEY

chics, Fl/ Division I
